</p><p>Circular business models, as the economic model more broadly, can have different emphases and various objectives, for example: extend the life of materials and products, where possible over multiple 'use cycles'; use a 'waste = food' approach to help recover materials, and ensure those biological materials returned to earth are benign, not toxic; retain the embedded energy, water, and other process inputs in the product and the material for as long as possible; Use systems-thinking approaches in designing solutions; regenerate or at least conserve nature and living systems; push for policies, taxes and market mechanisms that encourage product stewardship, for example 'polluter pays' regulations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Circular business models are enabled by circular supply chains. In practice, collaboration for circular supply chains can enable the creation, transfer, and/or capture of value stemming from circular business solutions. Collaboration in supply chains can extend to downstream and upstream partners, and include existing and new collaboration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sciencedirect.com&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciencedirect.com-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly, circular supply chain collaboration allows innovation into the circular business model, focusing on its processes, products, or services.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Digital_circular_economy">Digital circular economy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Digital circular economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Smart_circular_economy_framework.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Smart_circular_economy_framework.jpg/330px-Smart_circular_economy_framework.jpg" decoding="async" width="303" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Smart_circular_economy_framework.jpg/960px-Smart_circular_economy_framework.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="1640" /></a><figcaption>Smart circular economy framework<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kristoffersen-2020&#95;115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristoffersen-2020-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Building on circular business model innovation, <a href="/wiki/Digitization" title="Digitization">digitalization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">digital technologies</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">internet of things</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a>) are seen as a key enabler for upscaling the circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Data_economy" title="Data economy">data economy</a>, the central role of digital technologies for accelerating the circular economy transition is emphasized within the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Deal" title="European Green Deal">Circular Economy Action Plan</a> of the European Green deal. The smart circular economy framework illustrates this by establishing a link between digital technologies and sustainable resource management.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kristoffersen-2020&#95;115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristoffersen-2020-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This allows assessment of different digital circular economy strategies with their associated level of maturity, providing guidance on how to leverage data and analytics to maximize circularity (i.e., optimizing functionality and resource intensity). Supporting this, a Strategic Research and Innovation Agenda for circular economy was published in the framework of the <a href="/wiki/Horizon_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Horizon 2020">Horizon 2020</a> project CICERONE that puts digital technologies at the core of many key innovation fields (waste management, industrial symbiosis, products traceability).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some researchers have emphasised a need to comply with several requirements for implementing blockchain technology in order to make circular economy a reality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sadeghi-2022&#95;119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sadeghi-2022-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Platform_for_Accelerating_the_Circular_Economy_(PACE)"><span id="Platform_for_Accelerating_the_Circular_Economy_.28PACE.29"></span>Platform for Accelerating the Circular Economy (PACE)<span class="anchor" id="PACE"></span></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Platform for Accelerating the Circular Economy (PACE)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Resources_Institute" title="World Resources Institute">World Resources Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_MacArthur_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ellen MacArthur Foundation">Ellen MacArthur Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a>, and over 40 other partners launched the Platform for Accelerating the Circular Economy (PACE).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> PACE follows on the legacy of WEF's CEO-led initiative, Project MainStream, which sought to scale up circular economy innovations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> PACE's original intent has three focal areas:
</p>
<ol><li>developing models of <a href="/wiki/Blended_finance" title="Blended finance">blended finance</a> for circular economy projects, especially in developing and emerging economies;</li>
<li>creating policy frameworks to address specific barriers to advancing the circular economy; and</li>
<li>promoting <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public–private partnership">public–private partnership</a> for these purposes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ol>
<p>In 2020, PACE released a report with partner Circle Economy claiming that the world is 8.6% circular, claiming all countries are "developing countries" given the unsustainable levels of consumption in countries with higher levels of human development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>PACE is a coalition of CEOs and Ministers—including the leaders of global corporations like <a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">IKEA</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">Coca-Cola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/DSM_(company)" title="DSM (company)">DSM</a>, governmental partners and development institutions from Denmark, The Netherlands, Finland, Rwanda, UAE, China, and beyond.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Initiatives currently managed under PACE include the Capital Equipment Coalition with <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a> and numerous other partners<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Global Battery Alliance with over 70 partners.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In January 2019, PACE released a report entitled "A New Circular Vision for Electronics: Time for a Global Reboot" (in support of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/E-waste" class="mw-redirect" title="E-waste">E-waste</a> Coalition).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The coalition is hosted by a Secretariat headed by David B. McGinty, former leader of the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Innovation_Fund" title="Human Development Innovation Fund">Human Development Innovation Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palladium_International" title="Palladium International">Palladium International</a>, and board member of <a href="/wiki/BoardSource" title="BoardSource">BoardSource</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Board Members include <a href="/wiki/Inger_Andersen_(environmentalist)" title="Inger Andersen (environmentalist)">Inger Andersen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frans_van_Houten" title="Frans van Houten">Frans van Houten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_MacArthur" title="Ellen MacArthur">Ellen MacArthur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_P._Jackson" title="Lisa P. Jackson">Lisa P. Jackson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stientje_van_Veldhoven" title="Stientje van Veldhoven">Stientje van Veldhoven</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Circular_economy_standards">Circular economy standards</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Circular economy standards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="BS_8001:2017">BS 8001:2017</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: BS 8001:2017"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>To provide authoritative guidance to organizations implementing circular economy (CE) strategies, in 2017, the British Standards Institution (BSI) developed and launched the first circular economy standard "BS 8001:2017 Framework for implementing the principles of the circular economy in organizations".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The circular economy standard BS 8001:2017 tries to align the far-reaching ambitions of the CE with established business routines at the organizational level. It contains a comprehensive list of CE terms and definitions, describes the core CE principles, and presents a flexible management framework for implementing CE strategies in organizations. Little concrete guidance on circular economy monitoring and assessment is given, however, as there is no consensus yet on a set of central circular economy performance indicators applicable to organizations and individual products.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="ISO_59000_series">ISO 59000 series</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: ISO 59000 series"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a> (ISO) established a <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Organization_for_Standardization_technical_committees" class="mw-redirect" title="List of International Organization for Standardization technical committees">technical committee</a>, TC 323, to develop frameworks, guidance, supporting tools, and requirements for the implementation of activities of all involved organizations in the field of circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024 and 2025, the committee published a series of four new ISO standards:
</p>
<ul><li>ISO 59004:2024 Vocabulary, principles and guidance for implementation;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ISO 59010:2024 Guidance on the transition of business models and value networks;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ISO 59020:2024 Measuring and assessing circularity performance;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ISO 59040:2025 Product circularity data sheet.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Strategic_management_in_a_circular_economy">Strategic management in a circular economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Strategic management in a circular economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The CE does not aim at changing the <a href="/wiki/Profit_maximization" title="Profit maximization">profit maximization</a> paradigm of businesses. Rather, it suggests an alternative way of thinking how to attain a sustained <a href="/wiki/Competitive_advantage" title="Competitive advantage">competitive advantage</a> (SCA), while concurrently addressing the environmental and socio-economic concerns of the 21st century. Indeed, stepping away from linear forms of production most often leads to the development of new core competencies along the value chain and ultimately superior performance that cuts costs, improves efficiency, promote brand names, mitigate risks, develop new products,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and meets advanced government regulations and the expectations of green consumers. But despite the multiple examples of companies successfully embracing circular solutions across industries, and notwithstanding the wealth of opportunities that exist when a firm has clarity over what circular actions fit its unique profile and goals, CE decision-making remains a highly complex exercise with no one-size-fits-all solution. The intricacy and fuzziness of the topic is still felt by most companies (especially SMEs), which perceive circular strategies as something not applicable to them or too costly and risky to implement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This concern is today confirmed by the results of ongoing monitoring studies like the Circular Readiness Assessment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Strategic_management" title="Strategic management">Strategic management</a> is the field of <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a> that comes to the rescue allowing companies to carefully evaluate CE-inspired ideas, but also to take a firm apart and investigate if/how/where seeds of circularity can be found or implanted. Prior research has identified strategic development for circularity to be a challenging process for companies, demanding multiple iterative strategic cycles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-sciencedirect.com&#95;113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciencedirect.com-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The book <i>Strategic Management and the Circular Economy</i> defined for the first time a CE strategic decision-making process,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> covering the phases of analysis, formulation, and planning. Each phase is supported by frameworks and concepts popular in management consulting—like <a href="/wiki/Concept_map" title="Concept map">idea tree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Value_chain" title="Value chain">value chain</a>, <a href="/wiki/VRIO" title="VRIO">VRIE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porter%27s_five_forces_analysis" title="Porter&#39;s five forces analysis">Porter's five forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/PEST_analysis" title="PEST analysis">PEST</a>, <a href="/wiki/SWOT_analysis" title="SWOT analysis">SWOT</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> strategic clock, or the <a href="/wiki/Internationalization" title="Internationalization">internationalization</a> matrix—all adapted through a CE lens, hence revealing new sets of questions and considerations. Although yet to be verified, it is argued that all standard tools for strategic management can and should be calibrated and applied to a CE. A specific argument has already been made for the strategy direction matrix of product vs market and the <a href="/wiki/GE_multifactorial_analysis" title="GE multifactorial analysis">3 × 3 GE-McKinsey matrix</a> to assess business strength vs industry attractiveness, the <a href="/wiki/Growth%E2%80%93share_matrix" title="Growth–share matrix">BCG matrix</a> of market share vs industry growth rate, and Kraljic's portfolio matrix.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Engineering_the_circular_life_cycle">Engineering the circular life cycle</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Engineering the circular life cycle"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Product_lifecycle" title="Product lifecycle">Product lifecycle</a></div>
<p>In systems engineering, a '<a href="/wiki/Systems_development_life_cycle" title="Systems development life cycle">life cycle</a>' models the processes used to conceive, develop, produce, operate, support, and retire a system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ISO15288&#95;152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO15288-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NASA&#95;SEH&#95;153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_SEH-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-SEBoK&#95;Tailoring&#95;154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEBoK_Tailoring-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Particular acceptable approaches are sometimes designated in heavily regulated industries, such as in civil aviation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FAA&#95;AC20174&#95;155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAA_AC20174-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-RTCA&#95;DO178&#95;156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTCA_DO178-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-SAE&#95;ARP4754A&#95;157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAE_ARP4754A-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Complex and certified engineering systems, however, include many of the smaller products encountered on a daily basis, for example bicycles and household appliances.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_circular_lifecycle_for_complex_engineering_systems">The circular lifecycle for complex engineering systems</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The circular lifecycle for complex engineering systems"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Figure_4_Engineering_the_Circular_Lifecycle_A_conceptual_framework_for_applying_engineering_principles_for_circularity_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="&#39;Engineering the Circular Life Cycle: For Complex and Certified Systems. A framework for applying engineering principles to design and innovate for circularity." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Figure_4_Engineering_the_Circular_Lifecycle_A_conceptual_framework_for_applying_engineering_principles_for_circularity_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png/250px-thumbnail.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Figure_4_Engineering_the_Circular_Lifecycle_A_conceptual_framework_for_applying_engineering_principles_for_circularity_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png/500px-thumbnail.png 2x" data-file-width="2677" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>'Engineering the Circular Lifecycle: For Complex and Certified Systems. A framework for applying engineering principles to design and innovate for circularity.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Building on both the engineering lifecycle and the principles of the circular economy, the Circular Lifecycle for Complex Engineering Systems newly established framework, "<a href="/wiki/File:Figure_4_Engineering_the_Circular_Lifecycle_A_conceptual_framework_for_applying_engineering_principles_for_circularity_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png" title="File:Figure 4 Engineering the Circular Lifecycle A conceptual framework for applying engineering principles for circularity SAE INTERNATIONAL MELDRUM REBECCA 2023010988.png">Circular Lifecycle for Complex Engineering Systems</a>", forms the core of this approach. This framework advocates for a reassessment of recognized engineering disciplines with an emphasis on integrating less familiar circular principles. Not to be confused with diagrams depicting the flow of materials, the Lifecycle framework identifies the most important design principles. It has been expanded to highlight the key circular principles, for consideration at each stage of the Lifecycle, by the design engineers responsible for the designing, certifying, and modifying of the system.  It focuses on designing to meet user needs, the application of established engineering disciplines to achieve product longevity, engineering for the transition to renewable energy sources, and maximizing value generation from waste.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Meldrum-2023&#95;158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meldrum-2023-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As with the traditional engineering lifecycle, this framework for engineering the Circular Lifecycle, can be applied to all engineering systems. The depth of activity at each stage in the Lifecycle can simply be tailored based on the complexity of the product or system.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Lifecycle-value_stream_matrix">Lifecycle-value stream matrix</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Lifecycle-value stream matrix"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png/250px-The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png/500px-The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png 2x" data-file-width="2537" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>The life cycle - value stream matrix for a complex engineering system</figcaption></figure><p>The key to implementing the circular lifecycle for complex engineering systems is ensuring the engineering design team have a solid understanding of the product's ecosystem. The <a href="/wiki/File:The_life_cycle_-_value_stream_matrix_for_a_complex_engineering_systems_DESIGNING_AND_INNOVATING_FOR_CIRCULARITY_SAE_INTERNATIONAL_MELDRUM_REBECCA_2023010988.png" title="File:The life cycle - value stream matrix for a complex engineering systems DESIGNING AND INNOVATING FOR CIRCULARITY SAE INTERNATIONAL MELDRUM REBECCA 2023010988.png">Lifecycle-Value Stream Matrix for complex and certified circular systems</a> assists engineers and product design teams in visualizing the product's ecosystem more effectively.  
</p><p>The matrix captures the key value stream stakeholders, through the supply chain at the various levels of increasing complexity of system and equipment design. It is important to note that these suppliers will change throughout the life cycle. In the initial design phase of a complex engineering system the system-level design engineers would specify requirements and design the overall engineering system itself. As the high level design comes together, sub-system and equipment level suppliers are engaged and integrated into the platform and systems level design. Successful circular engineering principles are specified and designed within the overall platform requirements from the Innovate stage of the engineering lifecycle. As the engineering lifecycle continues, circular principles should continue to flow through the supply chain value stream, with each company challenging their suppliers to innovate and deliver products and services that facilitate circular operation and usage of the engineering system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Meldrum-2023&#95;158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meldrum-2023-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Adoption_and_applications_by_industry">Adoption and applications by industry</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Adoption and applications by industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Textiles">Textiles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Textiles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Circular_fashion" title="Circular fashion">Circular fashion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_fashion#Recycled_clothing" title="Sustainable fashion">Sustainable fashion §&#160;Recycled clothing</a></div>
<p>A circular economy for textiles embraces a broad spectrum of practices, including the sale of second‑hand clothing, garment‑rental services, repair of damaged apparel, collection and recycling of textile waste, and the design and production of garments intended for durability and made from recycled fibers.
</p><p>A circular textile economy is in response to the current linear model of the fashion industry, "in which raw materials are extracted, manufactured into commercial goods, and then bought, used, and eventually discarded by consumers" (Business of Fashion, 2017).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> '<a href="/wiki/Fast_fashion" title="Fast fashion">Fast fashion</a>' companies have fueled the high rates of consumption which further magnify the issues of a linear system. "The take-make-dispose model not only leads to an <a href="/wiki/Economic_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic value">economic value</a> loss of over $500 billion per year but also has numerous negative environmental and societal impacts" (Business of Fashion, 2018).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Such environmental effects include tons of clothing ending up in landfills and incineration, while the societal effects put human rights at risk. A documentary about the world of fashion, <i>The True Cost</i> (2015),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> explained that in fast fashion, "wages, unsafe conditions, and factory disasters are all excused because of the needed jobs they create for people with no alternatives." This shows that fast fashion is harming the planet in more ways than one by running on a linear system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>It is argued that by following a circular economy, the textile industry can be transformed into a sustainable business. A 2017 report, "A New Textiles Economy",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> stated the four key ambitions needed to establish a circular economy: "phasing out substances of concern and microfiber release; transforming the way clothes are designed, sold, and used to break free from their increasingly disposable nature; radically improving recycling by transforming clothing design, collection, and reprocessing; and making effective use of resources and moving to renewable input." While it may sound like a simple task, only a handful of designers in the fashion industry have taken charge, including <a href="/wiki/Patagonia_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Patagonia (clothing)">Patagonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Fisher" title="Eileen Fisher">Eileen Fisher</a>, Nathalia JMag, and <a href="/wiki/Stella_McCartney" title="Stella McCartney">Stella McCartney</a>. An example of a circular economy within a fashion brand is Eileen Fisher's Tiny Factory, in which customers are encouraged to bring their worn clothing to be manufactured and resold. Similar initiatives are also found in Europe, where outdoor garment companies facilitate a textile return systems that encourage customers to bring back used garments for repair, redesign, resale, or recycling.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Circular initiatives, such as clothing rental start-ups, are also getting more and more highlight in the EU and in the US as well. Operating with circular business model, rental services offer everyday fashion, baby wear, maternity wear for rent. The companies either offer flexible pricing in a 'pay as you rent' model like Palanta does,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or offer fixed monthly subscriptions such as <a href="/wiki/Rent_the_Runway" title="Rent the Runway">Rent The Runway</a> or <a href="/wiki/Le_Tote" title="Le Tote">Le Tote</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Research on the circular economy has highlighted the role of the informal sector in extending product life cycles. An Indian researcher from the Indian Institutes of Technology (IIT) has shown that street vendors contribute significantly to circular economy practices through the refurbishment and resale of second-hand clothing. However, the primary motivation for these vulnerable groups is not environmental sustainability, but livelihood generation. This phenomenon has been conceptualized as a <i>livelihood-driven circular economy</i> within the textile industry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Construction_industry">Construction industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Construction industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Deconstruction_(building)" title="Deconstruction (building)">Deconstruction (building)</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Concrete_recycling" title="Concrete recycling">Concrete recycling</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Modular_construction_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Modular construction systems">Modular construction systems</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Construction#Industry_scale_and_characteristics" title="Construction">construction</a> sector is one of the world's largest waste generators. The circular economy appears as a helpful solution to diminish the environmental impact of the industry.
</p><p>Construction is very important to the economy of the European Union and its state members. It provides 18 million direct jobs and contributes to about 9% of the EU's GDP.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The main causes of the construction's environmental impact are found in the consumption of non-renewable resources and the generation of contaminant residues, both of which are increasing at an accelerating pace.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the European Union alone, people and companies generate more than 2 billion tonnes of garbage year, or 4.8 tonnes per person, mostly from the building, mining, and manufacturing sectors.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EIB-2023&#95;15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIB-2023-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each individual in Europe generates half a tonne of municipal garbage annually, less than half of which gets recycled.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Cement production accounts for 2.4% of worldwide CO<sub>2</sub> emissions from industrial and energy sources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Decision making about the circular economy can be performed on the operational (connected with particular parts of the production process), tactical (connected with whole processes) and strategic (connected with the whole organization) levels. It may concern both construction companies as well as construction projects (where a construction company is one of the <a href="/wiki/Project_stakeholder" title="Project stakeholder">stakeholders</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Urban_decay" title="Urban decay">End-of-life buildings</a> can be deconstructed, hereby creating new construction elements that can be used for creating new buildings and <a href="/wiki/Land_recycling" title="Land recycling">freeing up space for new development</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Modular construction systems can be useful to create new buildings in the future, and have the advantage of allowing easier deconstruction and reuse of the components afterwards (end-of-life buildings).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Another example that fits the idea of circular economy in the construction sector on the operational level, there can be pointed <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnut</a> husks, that belong to hard, light and natural <a href="/wiki/Abrasives" class="mw-redirect" title="Abrasives">abrasives</a> used for example in cleaning brick surfaces. Abrasive grains are produced from crushed, cleaned and selected walnut shells. They are classified as reusable abrasives. A first attempt to measure the success of circular economy implementation was done in a construction company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The circular economy can contribute to creating new posts and economic growth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Górecki, one of such posts may be the Circular economy manager employed for construction projects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Automotive_industry">Automotive industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Automotive industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ecoleasing" title="Ecoleasing">Ecoleasing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_recycling" title="Vehicle recycling">Vehicle recycling</a></div>
<p>The circular economy is beginning to catch on inside the automotive industry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A case study within the heavy-duty and off-road industry<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schmitt-2021&#95;85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmitt-2021-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> analyses the implementation of circular practices into a lean manufacturing context, the currently dominant production strategy in automotive. Lean has continuously shown to increase efficiency by eliminating waste and focusing on customer value,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> contributing to eco-efficiency by narrowing resource loops. However, other measures are needed to slow down and close the resource loops altogether and reach eco-effectiveness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The study finds significant potentials by combining the lean and the circular approach, to not only focus on the product and process levels (eco-efficiency), but also on the system perspective (eco-effectiveness).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schmitt-2021&#95;85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmitt-2021-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are also incentives for carmakers to do so as a 2016 report by Accenture stated that the circular economy could redefine competitiveness in the automotive sector in terms of price, quality, and convenience and could double revenue by 2030 and lower the cost base by up to fourteen percent. So far, it has typically translated itself into using parts made from recycled materials,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> remanufacturing of car parts and looking at the <a href="/wiki/Ecodesign" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecodesign">design of new cars</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Remanufacturing is currently limited to provide spare parts, where a common use is remanufacturing gearboxes, which has the potential of reducing the global warming potential (CO<sub>2</sub>-eq) by 36% compared to a newly manufactured one.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the vehicle recycling industry (in the EU) only being able to recycle just 75% of the vehicle, meaning 25% is not recycled and may end up in <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> there is much to improve here. In the electric vehicle industry, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_robot" title="Industrial robot">disassembly robots</a> are used to help disassemble the vehicle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the EU's ETN-DEMETER project (European Training Network for the Design and Recycling of Rare-Earth Permanent Magnet Motors and Generators in Hybrid and Full Electric Vehicles) was researching the design of electric motors of which the magnets can be easily removed for recycling the rare earth metals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some car manufacturers such as Volvo are also looking at alternative ownership models (leasing from the automotive company; "Care by Volvo").<sup id="cite&#95;ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Logistics_industry">Logistics industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Logistics industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Globalize plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="Globe icon." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/60px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" decoding="async" width="48" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/120px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="290" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this section <b>may not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You may <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Circular_economy" title="Talk:Circular economy">talk page</a>, or create a new section, as appropriate.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The logistics industry plays an important role in the Dutch economy because the Netherlands is located in a specific area where the transit of commodities takes place on a daily basis. The Netherlands is an example of a country from the EU that has increasingly moved towards incorporating a circular economy given the vulnerability of the Dutch economy (as well as other EU countries) to be highly dependable on raw materials imports from countries such as China, which makes the country susceptible to the unpredictable importation costs for such primary goods.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:log&#95;188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:log-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Research related to the Dutch industry shows that 25% of the Dutch companies are knowledgeable and interested in a circular economy; furthermore, this number increases to 57% for companies with more than 500 employees. Some of the areas are chemical industries, wholesale trade, industry and agriculture, forestry and fisheries because they see a potential reduction of costs when reusing, recycling and reducing raw materials imports. In addition, logistic companies can enable a connection to a circular economy by providing customers incentives to reduce costs through shipment and route optimization, as well as, offering services such as prepaid shipping labels, smart packaging, and take-back options.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:log&#95;188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:log-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The shift from linear flows of packaging to circular flows as encouraged by the circular economy is critical for the sustainable performance and reputation of the packaging industry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Batista&#95;110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Batista-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The government-wide program for a circular economy is aimed at developing a circular economy in the Netherlands by 2050.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Several statistics have indicated that there will be an increase in freight transport worldwide, which will affect the environmental impacts of the <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">global warming potential</a> causing a challenge to the logistics industry. However, the Dutch council for the Environment and Infrastructure (Dutch acronym: Rli) provided a new framework in which it suggests that the logistics industry can provide other ways to add value to the different activities in the Dutch economy. Examples of adding value in innovative ways to the Dutch economy are an exchange of resources (either waste or water flows) for production from different industries and changing the transit port to a transit hub concept. The Rli studied the role of the potentials of the logistics industry for three sectors, agriculture and food, chemical industries and high tech industries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:log&#95;188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:log-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture"><span class="anchor" id="Agriculture&#95;industry"></span>Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">Sustainable agriculture</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Globalize plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="Globe icon." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/60px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" decoding="async" width="48" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/120px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="290" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this section <b>may not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You may <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Circular_economy" title="Talk:Circular economy">talk page</a>, or create a new section, as appropriate.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2019</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There has been widespread adoption of circular economic models in agriculture which is essential to global food security and to help mitigate against climate change, however there are also potential risks to human and environmental health from contaminants remaining in recycled water or organic material.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Carter-2024&#95;190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter-2024-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>These risks can be mitigated by addressing three specific issues that will also depend on the local context. These are contaminant monitoring, collection, transport, and treatment, and regulation and policy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Carter-2024&#95;190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carter-2024-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Netherlands, aiming to have a completely circular economy by 2050,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> intends a shift to circular agriculture <sup id="cite&#95;ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as part of this plan. This shift plans on having a "sustainable and strong agriculture" by as early as 2030.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Changes in the Dutch laws and regulations will be introduced. Some key points in this plant include:
</p>
<ul><li>closing the fodder-manure cycle</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Resource_recovery" title="Resource recovery">reusing</a> as much waste streams as possible (a team <i>Reststromen</i> will be appointed)</li>
<li>reducing the use of artificial fertilizers in favor of natural manure</li>
<li>providing the chance for farms within experimentation areas to deviate from law and regulations</li>
<li>implementing uniform methods to measure the <a href="/wiki/Soil_quality" title="Soil quality">soil quality</a></li>
<li>providing the opportunity to agricultural entrepreneurs to sign an agreement with the <i>Staatsbosbeheer</i> ("State forest management") to have it use the lands they lease for <i>natuurinclusieve landbouw</i> ("nature-inclusive management")</li>
<li>providing initiatives to increase the earnings of farmers</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Furniture_industry">Furniture industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Furniture industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>When it comes to the furniture industry, most of the products are passive durable products, and accordingly implementing strategies and business models that extend the lifetime of the products (like repairing and remanufacturing) would usually have lower environmental impacts and lower costs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Companies such as GGMS are supporting a circular approach to furniture by refurbishing and reupholstering items for reuse.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has seen a huge potential for implementing a circular economy in the furniture sector. Currently, out of 10,000,000 tonnes of annually discarded furniture in the EU, most of it ends up in landfills or is incinerated. There is a potential increase of €4.9 billion in Gross Value Added by switching to a circular model by 2030, and 163,300 jobs could be created.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A study about the status of Danish furniture companies' efforts on a circular economy states that 44% of the companies included maintenance in their business models, 22% had take-back schemes, and 56% designed furniture for recycling. The authors of the study concluded that although a circular furniture economy in Denmark is gaining momentum, furniture companies lack knowledge on how to effectively transition, and the need to change the business model could be another barrier.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Another report in the UK saw a huge potential for reuse and recycling in the furniture sector. The study concluded that around 42% of the bulk waste sent to landfills annually (1.6 million tonnes) is furniture. They also found that 80% of the raw material in the production phase is waste.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Oil_and_gas_industry">Oil and gas industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Oil and gas industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform#Repurposing" title="Oil platform">Oil platform §&#160;Repurposing</a></div>
<p>Between 2020 and about 2050, the oil and gas sector will have to decommission 600 installations in the UK alone. Over the next decade around 840,000 tonnes of materials will have to be recovered at an estimated cost of £25Bn. In 2017 North Sea oil and gas decommissioning became a net drain on the public purse. With UK taxpayers covering 50–70% of the bill, discussion of the most economic, social and environmentally beneficial decommissioning solutions for the general public may lead to financial benefits.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Organizations such as Zero Waste Scotland have conducted studies to identify areas with reuse potential, allowing equipment to continue life in other industries, or to be redeployed for oil and gas.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Renewable_energy_industry">Renewable energy industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Renewable energy industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">Energy transition</a></div>
<p>Oil and gas energy resources are incompatible with the idea of a circular economy, since they are defined as "development that meets the needs of the present while compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A sustainable circular economy can only be powered by renewable energies, such as wind, solar, <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>, and geothermal.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>What gives entities the ability to achieve 'net zero' carbon-emissions, is that they can offset their fossil fuel consumption by removing carbon from the atmosphere. While this is a necessary first step, global smart grid technologist, Steve Hoy, believes that in order to create a circular economy we should adapt the concept of 'True Zero' as opposed to 'net zero', which is eliminating fossil fuel consumption entirely so that all energy is produced from renewable sources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Current growth projections in the renewable energy industry expect a significant amount of energy and raw materials to manufacture and maintain these renewable systems. "Due to the emissions attributed to fossil-fuel electricity generation, the overall carbon footprint of renewable energy technologies is significantly lower than for fossil-fuel generation over the respective systems lifespan."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, there are still linear trajectories when establishing renewable energy systems that should be assessed in order to fully transition to a circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Reuter&#95;8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuter-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Education_industry">Education industry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education industry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2018, The Ellen MacArthur Foundation identified 138 institutions with circular economy course offerings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since then the theme of CE topics in teaching has been incorporated at a steadily increasing pace, with plans for adoption at university, city, and country wide levels.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-emf.thirdlight.com&#95;207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emf.thirdlight.com-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Circular&#95;economy&#95;in&#95;education&#95;208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circular_economy_in_education-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zero Waste Scotland is an example of a country wide program that plans to implement CE into the Scottish education system through the "YES Circular Economy Challenge" which advocates that "every learning environment should have a whole-environment approach to learning for sustainability that is robust, demonstrable, evaluated and supported by leadership at all levels".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Circular&#95;economy&#95;in&#95;education&#95;208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Circular_economy_in_education-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2021 report by the EMF compares London and New York CE course offerings and finds that there is not a "whole-environment" representation when it comes to different CE topics, with an element of the technical CE cycle being covered in 90% and element of the biological cycle covered in 50% of the 80 analyzed circular economy courses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-emf.thirdlight.com&#95;207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emf.thirdlight.com-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The EMF looks critically at the distribution of CE courses and researchers at Utrecht University Julian Kirchherr and Laura Piscicelli analyze the success of their introductory CE course in "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0921344919303015#!">Towards an Education for the Circular Economy (ECE): Five Teaching Principles and a Case Study</a>". With 114 published definitions for the Circular Economy, synthesis and collaboration, previously exemplified, could benefit and popularize CE application in higher education.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-emf.thirdlight.com&#95;207-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emf.thirdlight.com-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Plastic_waste_management">Plastic waste management</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Plastic waste management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable relarticle mainarticle selfreference noprint">This section is <a href="/wiki/Help:Transclusion" title="Help:Transclusion">transcluded</a> from <a href="/wiki/Plastic_pollution#Circular_economy_policies" title="Plastic pollution">Plastic pollution §&#160;Circular economy policies</a>. <span class="plainlinks" style="font-style: normal; font-size:85%;">(<a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plastic_pollution&amp;action=edit#Circular_economy_policies">edit</a> &#124; <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plastic_pollution&amp;action=history#Circular_economy_policies">history</a>)</span></div>
<p>Laws related to recyclability, waste management, domestic materials recovery facilities, product composition, biodegradability and prevention of import/export of specific wastes may support prevention of plastic pollution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A study considers producer/manufacturer responsibility "a practical approach toward addressing the issue of plastic pollution", suggesting that "Existing and adopted policies, legislations, regulations, and initiatives at global, regional, and national level play a vital role".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10.1016/j.heliyon.2020.e04709&#95;209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/j.heliyon.2020.e04709-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Standardization of products, especially of packaging<sup id="cite&#95;ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (January 2022)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which are, as of 2022, often composed of different materials (each and across products) that are hard or currently impossible to either separate or recycle together in general or in an automated way<sup id="cite&#95;ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> could support recyclability and recycling.
</p><p>For instance, there are systems that can theoretically <a href="/wiki/Waste_sorting" title="Waste sorting">distinguish between and sort</a> 12 types of plastics such as PET using <a href="/wiki/Hyperspectral_imaging" title="Hyperspectral imaging">hyperspectral imaging</a> and algorithms developed via <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while only an estimated 9% of the estimated 6.3<i>&#160;</i>billion tonnes of plastic waste from the 1950s up to 2018 has been recycled (12% has been incinerated and the rest reportedly being "dumped in landfills or the natural environment").<sup id="cite&#95;ref-economist.com&#95;216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Rare-earth_elements_recovery">Rare-earth elements recovery</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Rare-earth elements recovery"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable relarticle mainarticle selfreference noprint">This section is <a href="/wiki/Help:Transclusion" title="Help:Transclusion">transcluded</a> from <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth_element#Complications_of_recycling_and_reusing_REEs" title="Rare-earth element">Rare-earth element §&#160;Complications of recycling and reusing REEs</a>. <span class="plainlinks" style="font-style: normal; font-size:85%;">(<a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rare-earth_element&amp;action=edit#Complications_of_recycling_and_reusing_REEs">edit</a> &#124; <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rare-earth_element&amp;action=history#Complications_of_recycling_and_reusing_REEs">history</a>)</span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Circular economy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy#Conservation_areas,_recycling_and_rare-earth_elements" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy §&#160;Conservation areas, recycling and rare-earth elements</a></div>
<p>Despite the fact that e-waste contains a significant amount of rare-earth elements (REE), only 12.5% of e-waste is currently being recycled for all metals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Balaram2019&#95;217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balaram2019-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Main concerns about REE recycling and reuse include  environmental pollution during REE recycling and increasing recycling efficiency. Literature published in 2004 suggests that, along with previously established pollution mitigation, a more circular supply chain would help mitigate some of the pollution at the extraction point. This means recycling and reusing REEs that are already in use or reaching the end of their life cycle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ali&#95;123–134&#95;218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ali_123–134-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A study published in 2014 suggests a method to recycle REEs from waste <a href="/wiki/Nickel-metal_hydride_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickel-metal hydride batteries">nickel-metal hydride batteries</a>, demonstrating a recovery rate of 95.16%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
