</p><p>Rare-earth elements could also be recovered from industrial wastes with practical potential to reduce environmental and health impacts from mining, waste generation, and imports if known and experimental processes are scaled up.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A green system for recovery of REEs from coal fly ash has been developed using citrate and oxalate with strong organic ligands capable of precipitating REEs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2019 study suggests that "fulfillment of the circular economy approach could reduce up to 200 times the impact <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">in the climate change category</a> and up to 70 times the cost due to the REE mining."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2020, in most of the reported studies reviewed by a <a href="/wiki/Scientific_review" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific review">scientific review</a>, "secondary waste is subjected to chemical and or bioleaching followed by solvent extraction processes for clean separation of REEs."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
One study suggests that by 2050, up to 40 to 75% of the EU's clean energy metal needs could come from local recycling.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A study estimates losses of 61 metals, showing that use spans of, often scarce, <a href="/wiki/Technology-critical_element" title="Technology-critical element">tech-critical metals</a> are short.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A study using <a href="/w/index.php?title=Project_Drawdown&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Project Drawdown (page does not exist)">Project Drawdown</a>'s modeling framework indicates that, even without considering costs or bottlenecks of expansion of renewable energy generation, metal recycling can lead to significant <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Chemistry">Chemistry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Chemistry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_chemicals" title="Regulation of chemicals">Regulation of chemicals</a></div>
<p>Researchers have developed recycling-routes for 200 industrial <a href="/wiki/Chemical_waste" title="Chemical waste">waste chemicals</a> into important drugs and agrochemicals, for productive reuse that reduces disposal costs and hazards to the environment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A study has called for new molecules and materials for products with open-environmental applications, such as pesticides, that can be neither circulated nor recycled and provides a set of guidelines on how to integrate chemistry into a circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Circular_developments_around_the_world">Circular developments around the world</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Circular developments around the world"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Overview">Overview</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Overview"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Already since 2006, the European Union has been concerned about environmental transition issues by translating this into directives and regulations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Three important laws can be mentioned in this regard:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/European_Ecodesign_Directive" class="mw-redirect" title="European Ecodesign Directive">Ecodesign Framework Directive</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Waste_framework_directive" title="Waste framework directive">Waste Framework Directive</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Registration,_Evaluation,_Authorisation_and_Restriction_of_Chemicals" title="Registration, Evaluation, Authorisation and Restriction of Chemicals">Registration, Evaluation, Authorisation and Restriction of Chemicals Regulation</a></li></ul>
<p>On 17 December 2012, the European Commission published a document entitled "Manifesto for a Resource Efficient Europe".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EC-2013&#95;232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-2013-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2014, a zero-waste program for Europe has been put in place aiming at the circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since then, several documents on this subject have been published. The following table summarizes the various European reports and legislation on the circular economy that have been developed between 2014 and 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Volker-2020&#95;234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volker-2020-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In addition to the above legislation, the EU has amended the Eco-design Working Plan to add circularity criteria and has enacted eco-design regulations with circular economy components for 7 product types (refrigerators, dishwashers, electronic displays, washing machines, welding equipment and servers and data storage products).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Calisto&#95;Friant-2021&#95;235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calisto_Friant-2021-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These eco-design regulations are aimed at increasing the reparability of products by improving the availability of spare parts and manuals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Calisto&#95;Friant-2021&#95;235-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calisto_Friant-2021-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the same time, the European research budget related to the circular economy has increased considerably in the last few years: it has reached 964 million euros between 2018 and 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Volker-2020&#95;234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volker-2020-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In total, the European Union has invested 10 billion euros on Circular Economy projects between 2016 and 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Calisto&#95;Friant-2021&#95;235-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calisto_Friant-2021-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>One waste atlas aggregates some data about waste management of countries and cities, albeit the data is very limited.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The "Circularity Gap Report" indicates that "out of all the minerals, biomass, fossil fuels and metals that enter the <a href="/wiki/World_economy" title="World economy">world's economy</a>, only 8.6 percent are reused".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission's</a> <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Deal" title="European Green Deal">Circular Economy Action Plan</a> has resulted in a wide range of projects, with an emphasis on waste and material sustainability, as well as the circularity of consumer items. Despite a huge number of EU legislative measures, the European Union's circularity rate was 11.5% in 2022 and is slowing down currently.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Anyiego-2022&#95;36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anyiego-2022-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Programs">Programs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Programs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The "Manifesto for a Resource Efficient Europe" of 2012 clearly stated that "In a world with growing pressures on resources and the environment, the EU has no choice but to go for the transition to a resource-efficient and ultimately regenerative circular economy."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EC-2013&#95;232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-2013-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Furthermore, the document highlighted the importance of "a systemic change in the use and recovery of resources in the economy" in ensuring future jobs and competitiveness, and outlined potential pathways to a circular economy, in innovation and investment, regulation, tackling harmful subsidies, increasing opportunities for new business models, and setting clear targets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EC-2013&#95;232-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-2013-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_environmental_research_and_innovation_policy" title="European environmental research and innovation policy">European environmental research and innovation policy</a> aims at supporting the transition to a circular economy in Europe, defining and driving the implementation of a transformative agenda to green the economy and the society as a whole, to achieve a truly <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>. Research and innovation in Europe are financially supported by the program <a href="/wiki/Horizon_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Horizon 2020">Horizon 2020</a>, which is also open to participation worldwide.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Circular economy is found to play an important role to economic growth of European Countries, highlighting the crucial role of sustainability, innovation, and investment in no-waste initiatives to promote wealth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hysa&#95;et&#95;al&#95;2020&#95;53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hysa_et_al_2020-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union plans for a circular economy are spearheaded by its 2018 Circular Economy Package.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Historically, the policy debate in Brussels mainly focused on waste management which is the second half of the cycle, and very little is said about the first half: <a href="/wiki/Eco-design" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-design">eco-design</a>. To draw the attention of policymakers and other stakeholders to this loophole, the Ecothis, an EU campaign was launched raising awareness about the economic and environmental consequences of not including eco-design as part of the circular economy package.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2020, the European Union released its <a href="/wiki/Circular_Economy_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Circular Economy Action Plan">Circular Economy Action Plan</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="&quot;Closing_the_loop&quot;_(December_2015_–_2018)"><span id=".22Closing_the_loop.22_.28December_2015_.E2.80.93_2018.29"></span><i>"Closing the loop" (December 2015 – 2018)</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: &quot;Closing the loop&quot; (December 2015 – 2018)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>This first circular economy Action Plan consisted of 54 measures to strengthen Europe's global competitiveness, promote sustainable economic growth and create more jobs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ec.europa.eu&#95;243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among these 54 measures, for example, is the importance of optimizing the use of raw materials, products and waste in order to create energy savings and reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>. The main goal being in this respect to lead to the development of a framework conducive to the circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ec.europa.eu&#95;243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, the development of this Action Plan was also intended to enable the development of a new market for secondary raw materials. Concretely, here are the principal areas concerned by the Action Plan:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-McDowall&#95;et&#95;al&#95;2017&#95;244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDowall_et_al_2017-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Production</li>
<li>Consumption</li>
<li>Waste Management</li>
<li>Boosting markets for secondary materials</li>
<li>Innovation, investment and 'horizontal' measures</li>
<li>Monitoring progress</li></ul>
<p>The Action plan was also a way to integrate a policy framework, an integration of existing policies and legal instruments. It includes notably some amendments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-McDowall&#95;et&#95;al&#95;2017&#95;244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDowall_et_al_2017-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As a matter of fact, the implementation of this new plan was supported by the European Economic and Social Committee (EESC). This support included in-depth consultation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Circular_Economy_Action_Plan_of_2020"><i>Circular Economy Action Plan of 2020</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Circular Economy Action Plan of 2020"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>This new action was adopted by the European Commission in March 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EC-2020&#95;246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-2020-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A total of 574 out of 751 MEPs voted in favour of the action plan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It focuses on better management of resource-intensive industries, waste reduction, zero-carbonization and standardization of sustainable products in Europe.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EC-2020&#95;246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-2020-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prior to the development of this new action plan, we can also mention the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Deal" title="European Green Deal">Green Deal</a> of 2019, which integrated ecological and environmental ambitions to make Europe a carbon-neutral continent. On 10 February 2021, the European Parliament submitted its proposals to the Circular Economic Action Plan (CEAP) of the commission, highlighting five major areas in particular.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Those are the following:
</p>
<ul><li>Batteries</li>
<li>Construction and demolition</li>
<li>ICT</li>
<li>Plastics</li>
<li>Textiles</li></ul>
<p>Two additional sectors on which the CEAP focuses could be added: packaging &amp; food and water.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ranking_country_efforts">Ranking country efforts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Ranking country efforts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The European leaders in terms of circular economy are designated mostly by their current efforts for a shift towards circular economy but also by their objectives and the means implemented in this shift. It remains difficult to precisely rank how countries score in terms of circular economy, given the many principles and aspects of it and how differently one single country can score in each of these principles but some tendencies do appear in the average score, when combining the principles.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>: the government aims to reuse 50% of all materials as far as possible by 2030<sup id="cite&#95;ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and to convert waste into reusable materials anywhere it is possible. The next goal is then to make the country shift towards a 100% waste-free economy by 2050.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nl-2019&#95;251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nl-2019-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These objectives were all set from 2016 to 2019 in a series of programs for a governmental circular economy, raw materials agreements and transition agendas focusing on the five most important sectors for waste: biomass and food, plastics, manufacturing industry, construction and consumer goods.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>: Germany is a leader in some aspects of circular economy, like waste management and recycling.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> is also adding several texts and measures for a better circular economy in the country such as the roadmap for circular economy in 2018, consisting of 50 measures for a successful transition to circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> is also a consequent actor in the field. It scored second in the circular material use rate, before France but after the Netherlands.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Eurostat-2021&#95;254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-2021-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the other principles of circular economy, it usually scores in the top 5.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<p>Other notable countries are Italy, the United Kingdom, Austria, Slovenia, and Denmark.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Eurostat-2021&#95;254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat-2021-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Outside the EU, countries such as <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a> and especially <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> are working on the shift towards it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Most countries that are in the lead in the field of circular economy are European countries, meaning that Europe in general is in the lead group at the moment. The reasons behind this are numerous. First of all, circular economy is a field that is, at the moment mostly advanced in the developed countries, thanks to, between others, technology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The efforts of the European Commission are also non negligible, with documents such as the Commission staff working document "Leading the way to a global circular economy: state of play and outlook"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or the new action plan for circular economy in Europe,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> being one of the main blocs of the green deal.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Even if Europe as a whole is a good actor in the field, some European countries are still struggling to make the shift faster. These countries are mostly the eastern European countries (Romania, Hungary, Bulgaria, Slovakia, etc.) but also in some fields Portugal, Greece, Croatia and even Germany.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, the newspaper <a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico</a> made a ranking of the (by then) 28 European countries by making an aggregation of the seven key metrics of the commission for each country. The advantage here is that it gives a general view of how countries work towards circular development and how they compare to each other but the main drawback is that, as mentioned in the article, the seven metrics all have equal weight and importance in Politico's calculations, which is not the case in real life. Indeed, it is said in the same article that the countries that score the highest in CE are not necessarily the greenest according to the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, Germany, which scores 1st in the Politico ranking, only scores 13th worldwide in the EPI and is behind 10 European countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="China">China</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: China"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Beginning in the early 2000s, China started passing a series of laws and regulations to promote the circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhan-2022&#95;263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhan-2022-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 182–183">&#58;&#8202;182–183&#8202;</span></sup> In 2005, China's <a href="/wiki/National_Development_and_Reform_Commission" title="National Development and Reform Commission">National Development and Reform Commission</a> issued a policy document requiring maximization of recycling and reuse of wastewater, exhaust gas, and water residue generated during mining and smelting.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhou-2025&#95;264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhou-2025-264"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 12">&#58;&#8202;12&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>Policymakers' views expanded from a focus on recycling to broad efforts to promote efficiency and closed-loop flows of materials at all stages, from production to distribution to consumption.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhan-2022&#95;263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhan-2022-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 182">&#58;&#8202;182&#8202;</span></sup> As part of its efforts to enhance the circular economy, China is attempting to decrease its reliance on <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_China" title="Mining industry of China">mining for its mineral supply</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhan-2022&#95;263-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhan-2022-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 182">&#58;&#8202;182&#8202;</span></sup> Academic Jing Vivian Zhan writes that promoting the circular economy helps China to avoid the resource curse and helps to alleviate overreliance on extractive industries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhan-2022&#95;263-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhan-2022-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 182–183">&#58;&#8202;182–183&#8202;</span></sup>
</p><p>A major barrier to achieving a circular economy in China is poor enforcement of regulation, particularly at lower levels of government.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="European_Union">European Union</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: European Union"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Since 2015, there is a plan concerning the circular economy adopted by the European Commission. This first plan includes 54 actions. There are also 4 legislative proposals with the objective of legal change.
</p>
<dl><dd>a) the framework directive on waste</dd>
<dd>b) the directive on the landfill of waste</dd>
<dd>c) the directive on packaging and <a href="/wiki/Packaging_waste" title="Packaging waste">packaging waste</a></dd>
<dd>d) the directive on batteries and accumulators and their waste<sup id="cite&#95;ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>During the 2018 negotiations between the Parliament and the council, different elements will be adopted in four directives. These are mainly: «&#160;The main objectives are the following in the European framework
</p>
<ul><li>Minimum 65% of municipal waste to be recycled by 2035</li>
<li>Minimum 70% of all packaging waste to be recycled by 2030</li>
<li>Maximum 10% of municipal waste to be landfilled by 2035</li>
<li>Certain types of single use plastic will be prohibited to place on market as of July 2021</li>
<li>Minimum 32% of the Union's gross final consumption of energy to originate from renewable sources by 2030</li></ul>
<p>The main objectives are the following in the European framework.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2020, Europe's new green deal plan focuses on "design and production from the perspective of the circular economy",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Press&#95;corner&#95;268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press_corner-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> its main objective is to ensure that the European economy keeps these resources as long as possible.
The action plan of this circular development is mainly based on different objectives. They are:
</p>
<ul><li>"To make sustainable products the norm in the EU.</li>
<li>To empower consumers to choose.</li>
<li>Focusing on the most resource-intensive sectors with a high potential to contribute to the circular economy.</li>
<li>Ensure less waste."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Press&#95;corner&#95;268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press_corner-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Europe's green deal, which came into being in 2019, aims at a climate-neutral circular economy. For this, a distinct difference between economic growth and resources will be found. "A circular economy reduces the pressure on natural resources and is an indispensable prerequisite for achieving the goal of climate neutrality by 2050 and halting biodiversity loss."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Press&#95;corner&#95;268-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press_corner-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From 2019 to 2023, the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> funded €3.83 billion to co-finance 132 circular economy initiatives across many industries. Circular economy initiatives with a higher risk profile have secured finance through risk-sharing instruments and EU guarantees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Anyiego-2022&#95;36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anyiego-2022-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Benelux">Benelux</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Benelux"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Belgium">Belgium</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Belgium"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Since 2014, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> has adopted a circular strategy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>269<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is marked by 21 measures to be followed. In Belgium, the three Belgian regions (Flanders, Brussels and Wallonia) have different personal objectives. For Flanders, a strategy called Vision 2050 has been put in place.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>270<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For Wallonia, there is a plan following the declaration of the regional policy for Wallonia from 2019 to 2024. Since 23 January 2020, Wallonia has adopted a new strategy including three governance bodies: a steering committee, an intra-administration platform and an orientation committee.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>271<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
For Brussels, a plan was adopted in 2016 to develop the circular economy in its region. This plan will be in place for a period of 10 years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>272<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="The_Netherlands">The Netherlands</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: The Netherlands"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> set a plan of action for circular economy in 2016 and have been doing additional efforts for a transition towards a 100% circular economy by 2050 (and 50% by 2030). The Netherlands Organization for Applied Scientific Research estimates that a full shift towards Circular Economy will, at the long term, generate not less than 7.3 billion euros and 540,000 new jobs in the sector. The work will be developed around the five pillars mentioned above: plastics, biomass and food, the construction sector, the manufacturing industry, and consumer goods.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nl-2019&#95;251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nl-2019-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The government has also put a fund in place to facilitate and accelerate the shift. These funds are part of the 300 million € annually spent by the government for climate-related decisions and actions. The envelope is also completed by the ministry of infrastructure, which allocated €40 million for circular economy-related actions in 2019 and 2020. Other actions such as an allocation of subsidies for enterprises that make change or invest in the field have been taken. Initiatives at the subnational level are also encouraged and regions such as Groningen, Friesland, the Northern Netherlands, etc. ere taking actions to not only reduce their environmental impact but accelerate and accentuate their actions towards Circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>273<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Luxembourg"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>CE is one of the major deals of the 2018-2023 Luxembourg government.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> added in 2019 Circular economy in their data-driven innovation strategy, considering it now as a crucial field for innovation in the next years. It is present in most sectors of the country's development plan even if it is still only at the beginning of its development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>More initiatives are starting to emerge, however, to develop better in the field:
</p>
<ul><li>The 2019 "Circular economy strategy Luxembourg", a document testifying on the efforts made and to be made and the willingness to transform the Grand Duchy into an example in the field;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Holistic strategic studies such as the "strategic group for circular economy";<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Insertion of circular economy as a subject to be discussed by all the six main pillars of the "third industrial revolution";<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Creation of the Fit4Circularity program to allocate funds to innovative businesses in the field;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Participation in Circular economy-related events such as "Financing the circular economy" (2015) at the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> or the "Circular economy hotspot" (2017);<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Work on educational tools in the field;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Collaboration with municipalities, at the subnational level, to encourage them to become more circular;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lux-2019&#95;274-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lux-2019-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The establishment of value chains for local materials such as wood and a better management of raw materials in general;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>A cooperation between the public and the private sector;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The 'Product Circularity Data Sheet' (PCDS) launched in 2019 by the government to study and determine the circular potential of products and materials;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>An implementation of tools and methods such as a regulatory framework (laws), a financial framework (financial helps and sanctions), creation, management and sharing of knowledge on the subject, etc.;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>A coordination of the Luxembourg goals with the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">SDGs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2030_Agenda" class="mw-redirect" title="2030 Agenda">2030 agenda</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Schosseler-2021&#95;275-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schosseler-2021-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: United Kingdom"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Recycling_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Recycling in the United Kingdom">Recycling in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>In 2020, the UK government published its Circular Economy Package policy statement in coordination with the Welsh and Scottish governments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>277<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="England">England</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: England"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>From 1 October 2023, certain single-use plastic items have been placed under bans or restrictions in England.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>278<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Scotland">Scotland</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Scotland"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2021 the Scottish Parliament banned single use plastics being provided by businesses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>279<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2024, the Scottish Parliament passed the Circular Economy (Scotland) Act 2024, which would require the setting of targets and providing updates to the strategy to achieve those targets as frequently as 5 years or more frequently than that.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>280<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Wales">Wales</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Wales"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2021, the Welsh Government published its Circular Economy strategy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>281<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, the Senedd banned single use plastics, which would require the setting of targets and providing updates to the strategy to achieve those targets as frequently as 5 years or more frequently than that.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>282<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northern_Ireland">Northern Ireland</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Northern Ireland"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2022, the Northern Ireland Executive held a Circular Economy consultation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>283<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Circular_bioeconomy">Circular bioeconomy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Circular bioeconomy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bioeconomy" title="Bioeconomy">bio-economy</a>, especially the circular bio-economy, decreases dependency on natural resources by encouraging sustainable goods that generate food, materials, and energy using <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable biological resources</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Lupinus" title="Lupinus">lupins</a>). According to the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s EU Science Center, the circular bioeconomy produces €1.5 trillion in value added, accounting for 11% of EU GDP. The <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> invests between €6 billion and €9 billion in the bio-economy per year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EIB-2021&#95;284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIB-2021-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_European_Circular_Bioeconomy_Fund">The European Circular Bioeconomy Fund</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: The European Circular Bioeconomy Fund"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Eligibility requirements and core terms of reference for an equity and mezzanine debt fund were established by the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> directorates-general for agriculture and research and innovation. As a result, an investment adviser was chosen, and the European Circular Bioeconomy Fund was created.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>286<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>287<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2023, a €65 million investment from the EIB has been made.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EIB-2023&#95;15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIB-2023-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The European Circular Bioeconomy Fund invests in early-stage companies with developed innovations that are searching for funds to broaden their activities and reach new markets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>288<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>290<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-EIB-2021&#95;284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIB-2021-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It specifically invests in:
</p>
<ul><li>circular/bio-economy technologies,</li>
<li>biomass/feed stock production that boots agricultural productivity while lowering environmental impact,</li>
<li>biomass/feed stock technologies that result in higher-value, green goods,</li>
<li>bio-based chemicals and materials, and</li>
<li>biological alternatives in fields such as cosmetics.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-EIB-2021&#95;284-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIB-2021-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>291<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Circular_Carbon_Economy">Circular Carbon Economy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Circular Carbon Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>During the 2019 <a href="/wiki/COP25" class="mw-redirect" title="COP25">COP25</a> in Madrid, architect <a href="/wiki/William_McDonough" title="William McDonough">William McDonough</a> and marine ecologist <a href="/wiki/Carlos_M._Duarte" title="Carlos M. Duarte">Carlos Duarte</a> presented the Circular Carbon Economy at an event with the BBVA Foundation. The Circular Carbon Economy is based on McDonough's ideas from Carbon Is Not The Enemy<sup id="cite&#95;ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>292<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and aims to serve as the framework for developing and organizing effective systems for carbon management. McDonough used the Circular Carbon Economy to frame discussions at the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> workshops in March 2020 before the framework's formal acceptance by the G20 Leaders in November 2020.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Critiques_of_circular_economy_models">Critiques of circular economy models</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Critiques of circular economy models"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There is some criticism of the idea of the circular economy. As Corvellec (2015) put it, the circular economy privileges continued economic growth with soft "anti-programs", and the circular economy is far from the most radical "anti-program".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Corvellec (2019) raised the issue of multi-species and stresses "impossibility for waste producers to dissociate themselves from their waste and emphasizes the contingent, multiple, and transient value of waste".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Corvellec&#95;2019&#95;294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corvellec_2019-294"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 217">&#58;&#8202;217&#8202;</span></sup> "Scatolic engagement draws on Reno's analogy of waste as scats and of scats as signs for enabling interspecies communication. This analogy stresses the impossibility for waste producers to dissociate themselves from their waste and emphasizes the contingent, multiple, and transient value of waste".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Corvellec&#95;2019&#95;294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corvellec_2019-294"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 217">&#58;&#8202;217&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A key tenet of a scatolic approach to waste is to consider waste as unavoidable and worthy of interest. Whereas total quality sees in waste a sign of failure, a scatolic understanding sees a sign of life. Likewise, whereas the Circular Economy analogy of a circle evokes endless perfection, the analogy of scats evokes disorienting messiness. A scatolic approach features waste as a lively matter open for interpretation, within organizations as well as across organizational species.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Corvellec&#95;2019&#95;294-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corvellec_2019-294"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 219">&#58;&#8202;219&#8202;</span></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Corvellec and Stål (2019) are mildly critical of apparel manufacturing circular economy take-back systems as ways to anticipate and head off more severe waste reduction programs:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712" /><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Apparel retailers exploit that the circular economy is evocative but still sufficiently vague to create any concrete policies (Lüdeke‐Freund, Gold, &amp; Bocken, 2019) that might hinder their freedom of action (Corvellec &amp; Stål, 2017). Their business-centered qualification of take-back systems amounts to an engagement in "market action ... as leverage to push policymakers to create or repeal particular rules", as Funk and Hirschman (2017:33) put it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 26">&#58;&#8202;26&#8202;</span></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Research by Zink and Geyer (2017: 593) questioned the circular economy's engineering-centric assumptions: "However, proponents of the circular economy have tended to look at the world purely as an engineering system and have overlooked the economic part of the circular economy. Recent research has started to question the core of the circular economy—namely, whether closing material and product loops do, in fact, prevent primary production."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zink&#95;296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zink-296"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>296<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There are other critiques of the circular economy (CE).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>297<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>298<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, Allwood (2014) discussed the limits of CE 'material circularity', and questioned the desirability of CE in a reality with growing demand.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Allwood2014&#95;64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allwood2014-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The problem CE overlooks is how displacement is governed mainly by market forces, according to McMillan et al. (2012).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>299<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It's the tired old narrative, that the invisible hand of market forces will conspire to create full displacement of virgin material of the same kind, said Zink &amp; Geyer (2017).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zink&#95;296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zink-296"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>296<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Korhonen, Nuur, Feldmann, and Birkie (2018) argued that "the basic assumptions concerning the values, societal structures, cultures, underlying world-views and the paradigmatic potential of CE remain largely unexplored".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>300<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It is also often pointed out that there are fundamental limits to the concept, which are based, among other things, on the laws of <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">thermodynamics</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Reuter&#95;8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuter-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">second law of thermodynamics</a>, all spontaneous processes are <a href="/wiki/Irreversible_process" title="Irreversible process">irreversible</a> and associated with an increase in <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a>. It follows that in a real implementation of the concept, one would either have to deviate from the perfect reversibility in order to generate an entropy increase by generating waste, which would ultimately amount to still having parts of the economy which follow a linear scheme, or enormous amounts of energy would be required (from which a significant part would be dissipated in order to for the total entropy to increase).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>301<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In its comment to concept of the circular economy the European Academies' Science Advisory Council (EASAC) came to a similar conclusion:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712" /><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Recovery and recycling of materials that have been dispersed through pollution, waste and end-of-life product disposal require energy and resources, which increase in a nonlinear manner as the percentage of recycled material rises (owing to the second law of thermodynamics: entropy causing dispersion). Recovery can never be 100% (Faber et al., 1987). The level of recycling that is appropriate may differ between materials.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>302<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In addition to this, the circular economy has been criticized for lacking a strong <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a> component.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>303<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Indeed, most circular economy visions, projects and policies do not address key social questions regarding how circular economy technologies and solutions will be controlled and how their benefits and costs will be distributed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Calisto&#95;Friant-2020&#95;304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calisto_Friant-2020-304"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>304<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To respond to these limitations some academics and social movements prefer to speak of a circular society rather than a circular economy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Calisto&#95;Friant-2020&#95;304-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calisto_Friant-2020-304"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>304<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They thereby advocate for a circular society where knowledge, political power, wealth, and resources are sustainably circulated in fundamentally democratic and redistributive manners, rather than just improving resource efficiency as most circular economy proposals do.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>305<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Moreover, it has been argued that a <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_consumption#Degrowth" title="Sustainable consumption">post-growth approach</a> should be adopted for the circular economy where material loops are put (directly) at the service of wellbeing, instead of attempting to reconcile the circular economy with GDP growth.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>306<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, efficiency improvements at the level of individual products could be offset by a growth in total or per-capita consumption,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>307<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which only beyond-circularity measures like <a href="/wiki/Choice_editing" title="Choice editing">choice editing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rationing" title="Rationing">rationing</a> unsustainable products or emissions may be able to address.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Related_concepts">Related concepts</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Related concepts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The various approaches to 'circular' business and economic models share several common principles with other conceptual frameworks:
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Biomimicry">Biomimicry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Biomimicry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biomimicry" class="mw-redirect" title="Biomimicry">Biomimicry</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Janine_Benyus" title="Janine Benyus">Janine Benyus</a>, author of <i>Biomimicry: Innovation Inspired by Nature</i>, defined biomimicry as "a new discipline that studies nature's best ideas and then imitates these designs and processes to solve human problems. Studying a leaf to invent a better solar cell is an example. I think of it as 'innovation' inspired by nature".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>308<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Blue_economy">Blue economy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Blue economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Economy" title="The Blue Economy">The Blue Economy</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Economy" title="The Blue Economy">The Blue Economy</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Blue_economy" title="Blue economy">blue economy</a> usually refers to the "sustainable use of ocean resources for economic growth, improved livelihoods, and jobs while preserving the health of ocean ecosystem."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>309<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is focused on creating a human-marine balance that economically works while being regenerative and non-wasting.
</p><p>In their namesake <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Economy" title="The Blue Economy">2010 book</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Ecover" title="Ecover">Ecover</a> CEO and Belgian entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Gunter_Pauli" title="Gunter Pauli">Gunter Pauli</a> uses the term blue economy to refer to the societal shift to using materials of local abundance, choosing low-energy processes, and seeking to create revenue streams from each process step.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>310<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cradle_to_cradle">Cradle to cradle</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Cradle to cradle"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cradle_to_cradle_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Cradle to cradle design">Cradle to cradle design</a></div>
<p>Coined by Walter R. Stahel and popularized by the book <a href="/wiki/Cradle_to_Cradle:_Remaking_the_Way_We_Make_Things" title="Cradle to Cradle: Remaking the Way We Make Things">Cradle to Cradle: Remaking The Way We Make Things</a>, cradle to cradle (C2C) encourages organizations to adopt reuse and service-life extension of goods as a strategy for <a href="/wiki/Waste_prevention" class="mw-redirect" title="Waste prevention">waste prevention</a>, regional job creation, and <a href="/wiki/Resource_efficiency" title="Resource efficiency">resource efficiency</a> in order to decouple wealth from <a href="/wiki/Resource_consumption" title="Resource consumption">resource consumption</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-zhong&#95;311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zhong-311"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>311<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cooper-2005&#95;312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cooper-2005-312"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>312<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industrial_ecology">Industrial ecology</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Industrial ecology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Industrial_ecology" title="Industrial ecology">Industrial ecology</a></div>
<p>Industrial ecology is the study of material and energy flows through industrial systems. Focusing on connections between operators within the "industrial ecosystem", this approach aims at creating closed-loop processes in which waste is seen as input, thus eliminating the notion of undesirable by-product.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>313<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Resource_recovery">Resource recovery</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Resource recovery"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Resource_recovery" title="Resource recovery">Resource recovery</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Resource_recovery" title="Resource recovery">Resource recovery</a> is using wastes as an input material to create valuable products as new outputs. The aim is to reduce the amount of waste generated, therefore, reducing the need for <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a> space and also extracting maximum value from waste.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sound_Material-Cycle_Society">Sound Material-Cycle Society</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Sound Material-Cycle Society"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sound_Material-Cycle_Society" title="Sound Material-Cycle Society">Sound Material-Cycle Society</a></div>
<p>A similar concept used in Japan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>314<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Systems_thinking">Systems thinking</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Circular_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Systems thinking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Systems_thinking" title="Systems thinking">Systems thinking</a></div>
<p>The ability to understand how things influence one another within a whole. Elements are considered as 'fitting in' their infrastructure, environment and social context.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>315<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
